                  <hi rend="ital">A way, road,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">path;</hi> (S, M, Msb, K;) and <hi rend="ital">what is open,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conspicuous, thereof;</hi> (M, K;) and Er-Rághib adds, <hi rend="ital">wherein is easiness:</hi> (TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18820-1" target="سَبِيلَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n18822"/></foreign> signifies the same: (Ibn- 'Abbád, K:) the former is masc. and fem.; (S, M, Mgh, Msb, K;) like <foreign lang="ar">زُقَاقٌ</foreign>; (Msb;) made fem. by the people of El-Hijáz, and masc. by Temeem; (Akh, S voce <foreign lang="ar">زُقَاقٌ</foreign>;) but mostly fem.; (IAth, TA;) in the Kur it is made masc. in vii. 143, and fem. in xii. 108: (S, M, TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">سُبُلٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) or, accord. to ISk, it has this pl. when masc., and <foreign lang="ar">سُبُولٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">عُنُوقٌ</foreign> when fem., (Msb, [but this distinction and the latter pl. are both strange,]) and it has also as a pl. [of pauc.] <foreign lang="ar">أَسْبِلَةٌ</foreign>. (TA.) In the saying, <foreign lang="ar">وَ عَلَى ٱللّٰهِ قَصْدُ السَّبِيلِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And upon God it rests to show the right way</hi> (see art. <foreign lang="ar">قصد</foreign>)], (M, K,) in the Kur [xvi. 9], (M,) it is used as a gen. n., because it is added, <foreign lang="ar">وَ مِنْهَا جَائِرٌ</foreign>. (M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">اِبْنُ السَّبِيلِ</foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The son of the road;</hi> (M, K;) <hi rend="ital">he whom the road has brought,</hi> or [<hi rend="ital">as it were</hi>] <hi rend="ital">brought forth;</hi> (IB;) <hi rend="ital">the wayfarer,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">traveller:</hi> (Mgh, Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">he who travels much</hi> or <hi rend="ital">often:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">the traveller who is far from his place of abode:</hi> (Er-Rághib:) as used in the verse of the Kur, (M, Mgh, Msb,) ix, 60, (M,) it means <hi rend="ital">the person to whom the way has become cut short</hi> [<hi rend="ital">so that he is unable to continue his journey</hi>]; (M, K;) to which has been added, <hi rend="ital">who desires to return to his country,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">town, and finds not what will suffice him:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">the traveller who is cut off from his property:</hi> (Mgh, Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">the person who desires to go to a country,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">town, other than his own, for a necessary affair:</hi> or, accord. to Ibn-'Arafeh, <hi rend="ital">the guest who has become disabled from proceeding in his journey, his means having failed him:</hi> to such should be given as much as will suffice him to his home. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تَقْطَعُونَ السَّبِيلَ</foreign>, in the Kur [xxix. 28], means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">And ye cut off</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the way of offspring</hi> [by your unnatural practices]: or <hi rend="ital">and ye oppose yourselves to men in the roads</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">road</hi>] <hi rend="ital">for the purpose of that which is excessively,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">enormously, foul</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abominable.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">سَبِيلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The way,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cause, of God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of religion;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the way whereby one seeks approach to God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">advancement in his favour.</hi>] It is said in the Kur [ii. 191], <foreign lang="ar">وَ أَنْفِقُوا فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">And expend ye in warring against unbelievers</hi> and <hi rend="ital">the like,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">in every good work commanded by God;</hi> (M, K;) such being of the ways [that lead] to God: (M:) mostly used in relation to warring against unbelievers and the like. (M, K.) And in the same, iii. 163, <foreign lang="ar">ٱلَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">Who have been slain in the cause of God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of his religion,</hi> i. e.,] <hi rend="ital">for the sake of the religion of God.</hi> (Jel.) And you say, <foreign lang="ar">جَعَلَ ضَيْعَتَهُ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He made his estate to have its profit,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">revenue,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">usufruct, employed in the cause of God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of religion</hi>]. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سَبِيلٌ</foreign> also signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A means of access; a connexion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a tie:</hi> so in the saying, in the Kur [xxv. 29], <foreign lang="ar">يَا لَيْتَنِى ٱتَّخَذْتُ مَعَ ٱلرَّسُولِ سَبِيلًا</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">O would that I had obtained, with the Apostle, a means of access</hi> to Paradise]: (S, Msb, TA:) thus it has been explained: (TA:) or the meaning is, [<hi rend="ital">O would that I had taken, with the Apostle,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a way to safety:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">one way,</hi> the way of truth. (Bd.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  [Also, in the present day, applied to <hi rend="ital">A public drinking-fountain.</hi>]    </entryFree>26:Tb77,<entryFree id="n18811" key="سبّلهُ" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">Travelling upon a road:</hi> pl. <foreign lang="ar">سَوَابِلُ</foreign> and [coll. gen. n.]
